Project Obiectives
and DassrSition:    The main objective of the project would be to increase
and diversify production and incomes of farm families by
assisting Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments to
develop coastal lowlands, mudflats and shoals for culture
fisheries. The project would allow coastal dwellers to
switch to culture fisheries from the over-exploited
offshore fishing industry and to supplement their
earnings with livestock and horticultural activities.
The project would (a) develop mariculture by constructing
or improving about 10,100 ha of ponds for shrimp, eels
and laver (edible seaweed); (b) support animal husbandry
by providing breeding stock and on-farm improvements; (c)
promote agriculture by establishing fruit and nut
produetion bases; and (d) further the adoption of
technological advances by constructing pilot plants to
test new approaches in various fields of production and
processing. The project would Include support
facilities, such as feed sills, cold stores, processing
plants and brainlng centers, and local and overseas
training for technical and managerial staff and farmers.
eefits and Risks:  At full development, annual incremental production would
include 14,900 t of shrik-, 4,800 t of eels, 410 t of
dried laver, 130,000 minks, 1 million each of goats and
rabbits, 460,000 ducks and 1,2)0 t of fish, 43,000 t of
fruit and 18,200 t of nuts. Annual incremental output
from the project investment would be about Y550 zillion
(US$ 148 million). Earnings from project activities
would increase the per capita incomes of some 115,000
families by 15-35 percent. No major risks are
anticipated.

COASTAL LANDS DEVEOPMENT PROJECT
I. BACKGROUND
A. Introutio
1.1      The Government of China has requested Bank Group assistance in
financing development of coastal lands in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces.
The main component of the proposed project would be development of
mariculture--shrimp, eel and laver (an edible seaweed)--on coastal
lowlands, mudflats and shoals and provision of support facilities, such as
feed mills, cold stores, and technical service centers. The project would
also include in Jiangsu Province small components for expansion of
livestock and horticultural production in the coastal region,
agroprocessing plants, and adoption of technological innovations in
agriculture, mariculture and livestock. The project covers three
municipalities, administratively responsible for 17 counties, in Jiangsu
and 18 counties in Zhejiang. The initial proposal, presentedt by the State
Planning Commission (SPC) in August 1986, was confined to Jiangsu
Province. The project scope was subsequently expanded to include
developing coastal lands for mariculture in Zhajiang Province. The
project areas were visited by a Preappraisal Mission in March 19F7 and the
project was appraised in June 1987.
B. The Agricultural Sector
1.2      Agriculture in China provides sustenance to over one billion
people and is an important source of income for some 190 million farm
families and accounts for about 35% of the country's GDP. Only about 137
million ha of China's land area of 960 million ha are arable. Farming
systems are intensive, with large inputs of labor, chemical and organic
fertilizers, and water. Nearly half of the arable land is irrigated.
Foodgrains occupy about 70% of the cropland and account for about
one-third of total agricultural output. This intensive system of food
production allows China to meet the basic food requirements of its
population (about 22% of the world's total) from less than 8% of the
world's arable land.
1.3      Major reforms in farm policies since 1979, especially a shift
from collective to household farming and increases in farm prices, have
led to rapid growth and diversification in agricultural production. This
shift has given farmers more flexibility in determining what crops to
grow, how wuch to produce, and where to market their output. Results have
been dramatic: production increased by about 10% per year over the period
1980-85 in comparison with an average of 3% per year in the preceding 23
years. Grain output reached a record 407 million t in 1984, 34% greater
than in 1978, despite a reduction in the area sown with grains. In 1985,
the Government began a new phase of reform, replacing compulsory
procurement quotas with voluntary contracts, adjusting procurement prices,
and greatly enlarging the role of the market. These measures contributed
to a decline in grain and cotton area and output as farmers increasingly
shifted production into livestock, aquaculture and industrial crops. As



- 2 -
the current reforms are extended, the challenge to China's agriculture
will be to maintain an adequate growth rate while continuing to provide
both basic grain security and diversified consumption patterns. In terms
of the average Chinese diet, Chinese planners project a rapid increase in
the demand for fruits, vegetables, meat, poultry, fish and dairy products
with a corresponding decrease in the share of direct grain consumption.
C. The Fisheries Subsector
1.4      China's fisheries subsector, including culture and capture
production from marine and freshwater sources, accounts for about 1.5% of
the gross value of agricultural output (GVAO). Total fisheries production
increased from 5.3 million t in 1983 to 8.0 million t in 1986, an increase
of 50%. The output of capture fisheries has reached a plateau of about
3.5 million t per year and is expected to remain at this level through the
year 2000, since both coastal and inland waters are being fully
exploited. Government policy since the early 1980s has aimed toward
shifting the production structure from capture to culture fisheries to
achieve growth in output. China has some 5 million ha of freshwater
bodies and 1.3 million ha of coastal waters which are suitable for
aquaculture, of which about 3 million ha (60%) and 293,000 ha (220),
respectively, are at present being used. The existence of extensive
unutilized areas suitable for culture fisheries and the fact that
significant increases in yields may be realized through application of new
technology and management methods led the Government to adopt in the early
1980s an ambitious program to expand annual fisheries production to 11
million t by the year 2000; current production levels confirm that this
target is attainable.
D. Coastal Land Development
1.5      Geographically, Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces are ideally
situated to develop their coastal lands for intensive fish culture: they
have a combined shoreline of more than 3,000 km; both provinces have rich
natural resources of eel fry and brood shrimp; water quality is good; and
considerable local experience has been gained over the last five years in
fishery technology, particularly in shrimp production techniques. Jiangsu
has the unique topographic feature of an expanding coastline, formed from
silt carried by the river flow to the mouth of the Yangtze River, then
picked up and driven north by tidal currents. Local governments have
periodically constructed embankments for the purpose of extending the
cultivable area and affording it flood protection from monsoon storms.
Zhejiang, which has an irregular, mountainous coastline, carries out land
reclamation by erecting dikes to connect adjacent promontories at their
bases. In both provinces, most of the coastal land development schemes
have focussed on expansion of culture fisheries for both marine and
freshwater aquatic products. However, the local governments have faced
financial and technological constraints which resulted in the land being
used for low-yielding extensive cultivation. Ponds are shallow ard
irregularly shaped, water control facilities are crude, and the degrue of
mechanization is low. Production is limited by lack of quality formulated
feed and farmers' access to fry, and output value is diminished by
inadequate freezing and preservation capacity and crude processing
technology.



. 3 -
E. Sectoral Objectives and Bank Lending
1.6      The Government's long-term objectives for the agricultural sector
are (a) to increase the production of food, feed and industrial crops to
meet requirements created by population and income growth, and (b) to
raise incomes and employment opportunities 'n rural areas. Given China's
shortage of arable land (0.1 ha per capita), development planners have
focussed on the need to increase the productivity of existing cropped
areas and to develop efficiently the few remaining areas of unutilized
land. Steps are also being taken to stabilize food grain output at the
1983 level, increase production and quality of animal feed, livestock,
fruit, fish, and industrial crops, and expand agro-processing &.; 'vities
so as to raise the value-added in the farm sector. Improved prc.ucer
incentives include (a) contract systems which permit household-level
management within both collective and state-owned farm sectors; (b)
continued expansion of the market; (c) adjustment of producer prices; and
(d) establishment of private, public and mixed enterprises in rural
agro-processing, transport and commerce. For the fisheries sector, rne
Government's objectives are to increase production for domestic
consumption, provide additional income sources for the rural populationL,
and gain foreign exchange earnings from the export of high-valued aquatic
products such as shrimp, eel and laver /1. The development strategy
emphasizes establishment of fish culture systems on land unsuitable for
crop cultivation--freshwater culture on swamps, marshes and poorly drained
interior land and marine culture on coastal lowlands, shoals and mudflats.
1.7      The Bank's lending to China's agricultural sector has supported
the Government efforts to raise and diversify agricultural production
through more efficient: use of land, water and labor resources and through
improvement of support ax-vices such as credit, research and agricultural
education.  Past lending to .he sector has focussed on land reclamation
and development--North China Plain (Cr. 1261-CHA) and Heilongjiang Land
Reclamation (Ln. 2261-CHA)-- mad strengthening agricultural support
services--Agriculture Lhut-.Won and Research (Cr. 1297-CHA), the Second
Agricultural Research Project (Cr. 1516-CHA), three rural credit projects
(Cr. 1462-CHA, Cr. 1642-CHA, and Cr. 1871-CHA) and the Seeds Project (Cr.
1577-CHA). Projects of the specialized product subsector type include the
Forestry Development Project (Cr. 1605-CHA), the Freshwater Fisheries
Project (Cr. 1689-CHA), and the Rubber Development Project (Cr.
1417-CHA/SF 5-CHA).  The area development approach, which generally
targets difficult development problems, combines in a single project
assistance to land development and support services previously the subject
of separate projects. It takes advantage of the close integration of
governmental functions at the local level in China, which facilitates
inter-agency cooperation. The Pishihang-Chaohu Area Development Projecc
(Ln. 2479/Cr. 1606-CHA) was the first of this type, followed by Red Soils
Area Development Project (Cr. 1733-CHA), the Xinjiang Area Development
/1 Laver is a seaweed product, widely known by its Japanese name "nori".
It is used as a wrapping for sushi and is a popular soup ingredient in
Oriental cuisine.



- 4 -
Project (Cr. 1764-CHA) and the Gansu Area Development Project
(Cr. 1793-CHA). Implementation of most ongoing Bank Group-financed
projects in the agriculture sector is on schedule. Notable features of
all the projects are the high standard of management at the central,
provincial and county levels and the enthusiastic participation of the
collectives and farmers.
F. Project Formulation and Rationale
1.8      The SPC has proposed the Coastal Lands Development Project for
Bank financing. As part of the Government's efforts toward
decentralization, this project would be implemented by the two provinces
without direct involvement of line ministries at the central level. Both
provinces have primarily focussed on aquaculture activities which
represent the most economically and financially attractive uses of coastal
lowlands and shallow waters, e.g., shrimp, eel and lav%1r production. To
diversify production, Jiangsu has also selected specialized horticultural
and livestock activities which take best advantage of available natural
resources in the coastal regions and, in some cases, are complementary to
mariculture. Moreover, to streamline research, development and commercial
application of innovative technological advances, the project will provide
funding in Jiangsu Province for an agricultural technology development
component. The component consists of eight subprojects for
commercialization of technological developments in production, processing
and utilization of mariculture, mink, field and vegetable crops. The
project would support the Government's overall objectives for the
agricultural sector and the fisheries subsector. It would serve as a
model for future development of similar land areas within the two
provinces and in other provinces bordering the sea. The Bank Group's
primary contribution to the project involves drawing on the experience of
its staff and consultants to improve the technology, design, organization
and implementation of the project.  This includes provision of assistance
during and after project preparation to insure appropriate selection of
sites and technology based on technical, financial and economic
considerations; coordinated planning of aquatic production, animal
husbandry and agro-processing components; assessment of local and export
market potential for the main aquatic products; and access to advanced
technology.



- 5 -
II. THE PROJECT AREAS
A. L*eati&n
2.1      The proposed project would be carried out in the coastal regions
of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, which are neighboring provinces lying immediately
to the north and south, respectively, of Shanghai. The Jiangsu component
would be located in 17 counties and districts under the jurisdiction of
the coastal municipalities of Lianyungang, Nantong, and Yancheng; the
project area includes 73 townships and 970 villages, with a total
population of 1.4 million. Even though the major emphasis of tha project
would be mariculture (shrimp, eel and laver production), many of the
participating counties would be involved in more than one production
activity. For example, Yancheng would also include animal husbandry and
orchard development and Lianyungang, fruit and nut production. The
Zhejiang component would involve shrimp and eel production and would be
located in 18 counties and four small- to medium-size cities, including an
island county about 65 km offshore. The population in the project areas
totals 2.2 million. Project locations are shown in IBRD Maps 20260 and
20261.
B. Climate
2.2      Located between 30 and 35 degrees north latitude, Jiangsu lies at
the transition point between temperate and subtropical climates. Aver%ge
daily temperatures range from a January low of 2 degrees C. to a high of
29 degrees C. in July and August. Rainfall averages between 1,000 and
1,100 mm per year, with about two-thirds occurring in the May-September
period. The frost-free period ranges from 200 to 240 days per year and
evaporation is between 1,400 to 1,600 mm per annum. Wind speeds are
generally low except during typhoons which affect the areas for about 7-20
days annually; during these periods, winds exceed 17 m/sec.
2.3      Zhejiang, situated between 27 and 31 degrees north latitude, has
a somewhat milder climate than Jiangsu with average daily temperatures
ranging from 5 degrees C. in January to 28 degrees C. in July and August.
Rainfall averages 1,000 to 1,600 mm per year. The frost-free period
ranges from 250 to 310 days per year and evaporation is 1,200 to 1,600 mm
per year.
2.4      Since shrimp culture in seawater would be the main project
activity and since shrimp growth is limited to conditions of 15 to 30
degrees C, seawater temperature is a critical factor in production.
Seawater temperatures in Jiangsu, ranging from 4 to 27 degrees C., allow a
five-month growing period from late May to late October. The growing
period is about two weeks longer in Zhejiang.
C. CoastAl TgoograDhy and Soils
2.5      The coastal area of Jiangsu is profoundly influenced by the
Yellow and Yangtze Rivers. The Yangtze River brings vast quantities of
sediment into the coastal zone and deposition of this sediment has an
ongoing influence on the coastline. £he Yellow Sea, sheltered in the east
and northeast by Korea and Japan, receives the dominant part of its wave



6-
energy from the southeast. Littoral drift of sediment, under the
influence of wave action and tidal currents, is principally northward
along the Jiangsu coast. These processes result in high silt
concentrations in the coastal waters and accretion of as much as 200-300 m
per year in some locations. A thousand-year-old coastal embankment,
built to protect lowlands from flooding during storm tides, is now 50 km
inland from the shore. In the last three decades, new embankments have
been built for flood protection every ten years or so, and land inside has
become a base for production of cotton and grain. The land to be
developed for shrimp production under the project is within tta protection
of existing sea dikes on the most recently reclaimed land. Because of the
character of the landforms, topographic relief is no more than a few
meters. The shoreline slope is very flat; at low tide the water line in
some areas is 10 km offshore. Marine satling directions warn shipping of
hazards from migrating shoals within 80 km of the coast.
2.6      In historic times, the Yellow River invaded the Huai River and
for about 700 years formed an outlet through Jiangsu creating a delta
between Lianyungang and Yancheng. In the mid 18009, the river resumed its
earlier course, leaving the land referred to as the "Old Yellow River Bed"
as one of the distinctive features of the province. This area would be
developed to orchards and vineyards under the proposed project.
2.7      Soils in the Jiangsu coastal areas consist of various fine sands,
silts and clays. Groundwater and soil salinity at the toe of the sea dike
(on the sea side) are about 1  and 2-4%, respectively.  Behind the sea
dike, soil salinity gradually declines and organic content increases as
the land becomes colonized by salt tolerant vegetation. The land to be
developed for shrimp farming, located immediately inside the most recent
sea dikes, is for the most part unused and currently unsuitable for crop
cultivation. In some areas, shallow evaporation ponds for recovering salt
from seawater are in use. The development of shrimp ponds is seen as a
step in a progression of land usAs leading to freshwater aquaculture and
eventually to desalination of the soil and diverse agricultural
activities. Land to be used for laver cultivation is in the intertidal
zone outside the embankments where the only alternative commercial
activity would be harvesting of shellfish. Eel farms are built on
low-value land with suitable water supplies; some sites are on coastal
land adjacent to shrimp or laver cultivation sites and some are inland.
Animal husbandry would be practiced on land of low productivity adjacent
to the coastal zone.
2.8      In Zhejiang, a mountainous province, the coastal region features
a rocky shoreline with numerous islands and small bays. Some areas of low
land in Hangzhou Bay are affected by progressive accretion, but most of
the coastline is neither accreting nor eroding at a significant rate. The
lands which would be reclaimed are tidal flats in coves and between
islands along the rocky coastline. The soil on these tidal flats is soft
marine clay with a very high water content. In some areas, the bearing
strength is less than one ton/sq m. Provincial engineers are experienced
in the special problems involved in excavating this marine clay and
building safe structures on such foundations. Eel culture would generally
be located inland on coastal wasteland and other low-lying land.



-7-
D. Infrastructure
Irrigation and Drainage Works
2.9      The coastal regions of Jiangsu province are equipped with an
extensive network of irrigation, drainage and transportation canals linked
to the Yangtze River. Numerous gate structures control water movements
and the release of drainage water to the sea through the sea dikes. Most
of the proposed shrimp farms lie adjacent to irrigated areas and,
therefore, would have access to supplies of fresh water as well as sea
water.
2.10     Although Zhejiang province is mountainous, water resources in the
valleys and on the small coastal planes are highly developed with
extensive networks of irrigation and transportation canals.
Transportation from sites of shrimp pond development would be via seaports
with easy access to several major cities.
Power and Transport
2.11     Rural electrification in both provinces is extensive.  In
Jiangsu, water pumping in existing projects is powered electrically,
though electricity shortages are common in the province. In the long
range plans for Jiangsu province, top priority--ahead of either
agriculture or transport--is being given to expansion of electricity
supply. The three coastal cities all have new generating stations under
construction which will double or triple their existing capacities.
Lianyungang is expanding an existing coal-fired plant, Nantong is
increasing the capacity of the Tianshengang station, and Yancheng is
installing a new 125 MW unit to supplement the existing 68 NW plant. The
magnitude of the project needs is, relatively speaking, not large, and in
the agricultural season, even cities shed electrical load to permit an
adequate supply for key activities. The Planning and Economic Commission
of Jiangsu has stated that electricity supply for the project will be
guaranteed.
2.12     In Zhejiang, all project sites are accessible to the provincial
power grid.  Little pumping of seawater would be required for shrimp
cultivation, givea the high tidal range. Some pumping of drainage flows
would, however, be required and both electric and diesel power pumps would
be included in the project.
2 13     The improvement of transportation infrastructure is one of the
top three priorities of the Government's strategy for development in
Jiangsu. However, the existing system, while congested, will not be a
limiting factor in the success of the project. All project sites are
accessible by road. Generally, roads along the sea dikes have become
principal regional access routes. Heavy goods are carried mainly by
barges on the canals. In Zhejiang, the coastal areas are served by an
adequate road network. A considerable amount of highway construction,
including tunnelling to bypass some of the steepest mountain passes, is
under way along the access routes to the project areas. The population
density and character of the terrain suggest that congested road
conditions can be expected for many years. However, an alternative



. 8 -
exists in the form of sea transport which is used to carry goods to and
from other regions and also locally, for example, within a construction
site. The project areas utilize sea, rail or road routes to major cities,
and hence to the export markets abroad. Lianyungang in Jiangsu and Ningbo
and Hangzhou in Zhejiang have regularly scheduled air service to Shanghai,
an international airport.
E. Status of Mariculture
2.14     Jiangsu's fisheries output in 1986 of 805,000 tons ranked fifth
among Chiua's provinces. This output was composed mostly of freshwater
fisheries (67%) and capture sea fishing (30%). Nariculture (cultivation
of marine species) amounted to only 3% of output. Jiangsu has only one
shrimp hatchery, in Lianyungang, but its capacity of tour billion seeds
per year is adequate to supply project needs. P:ovincial production of
eel fry, which exreds 10 t per year, is the greatest in China.
Zhejiang's fisheries output in 1986 was 1.2 million t. Its capture sea
production of 850,000 t, mostly from the fertile Zhoushan Archipelago,
placed it first in China. However, capture fishing faces problems of
depletion and unreliable yields. Therefore, both project provinces are
developing higher-yielding mariculture along their newly reclaimed coastal
land and on intertidal mudflats.
F. Training. Research and Extension
2.15     Both provinces have well-established institutional structures for
research, extension and training, some of which will be strengthened under
the project to cope with the expanded production facilities. Foremost
among the provincial aquaculture training centers in Jiangsu is the
Lianyungang Aquaculture School, renowned nationally for its three-year
secondary-level technical school which produces some 200 graduates each
year. Two facilities--the Nanjing Agricultural Institute and the Suzhou
Silk Institute--offer four-y'ear univerAity level aquaculture training and
have some 150-200 graduates annually. In addition, the Nanjing
Aquaculture Staff Academy offers six-month and one-year continuing
education programs. The Zhejiang Fishery College, with branches in Ningbo,
Xiaoshan and Zhoushan, is the main higher-level education facility in
Zhejiang province.  The Zhejiang Marine Fishery Research Institute in
Zhoushan, the Niw;bo Municipal Fishery Research Institute, and the
Zhejiang Fishery College have ongoing research programs in shrimp feed
formulation and will be contracted under the proposed project to develop
feed formulations for specific areas.



III. THE PROJECT
A.  Prolect Objectives and Relation to Sector
3.1     The main objective of the proposed project would be to ass:.st the
Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provincial Governments to develop coastal lowlands,
mudflats and shoals for culture fisheries. The project would allow
coastal dwellers to switch from the already over-exploited offshore
fishing industry to mariculture and to supplement their earnings with
livestock and specialized agricultural activities. This objective is in
line with the Central Government's objective to expand fisheries
production and increase rural incomes, mainly through the development of
culture fisheries on agriculturally unproductive land. The development of
shrimp ponds in the Jiangsu coastal areas is expected to be a step in a
progression of land uses leading later to freshwater aquaculture and
eventually to desalination of the soil and diversification of agricultural
activities as the coastline builds up and present sites become further
inland.
B. Prolect Descrigtion
3.2     The proposed project would develop coastal land in Jiangsu and
Zhejiang provinces, mainly for cultivation of shrimp, eel and laver.  In
addition to the core mariculture activities, it would include components
for animal husbandry and horticulture, each with associated
agro-processing facilities (Table 3.1), and a component for adoption of
newly developed technological advances aimed at providing solutions to
existing production problems in the project areas and elsewhere in China.
3.3     In Jiangsu, t i proposed project would be carried out in 17
counties under the administrative jurisdiction of three coastal cities:
Lianyungang, Nantong and Yancheng. To diversify production and provide
additional income to farm families, Jiangsu has selected specialized
agricultural and livestock production for development as sideline
activities. These include production of fruits adapted to the coastal
climate and suitable for growing on the adjacent hilly terrain, small
ruminants to take advantage of the abundance of wild grasses growing near
the sea, ducks and fish to maximize utilization of pond areas, and mink to
utilize byproducts from meat processing and trash fish from the coastal
fishery industry. The main features of the project are:
(a) Nariculture - construction or improvement of about 8,260 ha
of ponds for shrimp, 33 ha of open ponds and 87,000 sq m of
sheltered ponds for eels, establishment of about 275 ha of
laver fields, and provision of supporting facilities (nine
hatcheries, three technical service centers, 13 feed mills,
14 cold stores and laver processing equipment) and production
materials; site locations are listed in Annex 1, Table 1;
(b) Animal husbandr - provision of breeding stock and on-farm
improvements for development of goat, duck, rabbit and mink
production; construction and equipping of six agro-processing
plants, three feed mills, and one training center;

(d) Agriculture Technology Development - establishment of three
feed mills, four processing plants for rapeseed, sesbania,
asparagus and barley malt, a facility to produce serology
test kits, and 18,000 ha of field and vegetable crops.
3.4     In Zhejiang, the proposed project would include shrimp and eel
production in areas administered by a number of local governments, but
under the umbrella of a provincial bureau. Five sites would be developed
for shrimp and 18 for eel. The main features of the project in Zhejiang
province are:
Mariculture - construction of about 1,380 ha of ponds for
shrimp and 118 ha of open ponds and 150,000 sq m of sheltered
ponds for eels; provision of supporting facilities (three
hatcheries, five cold stores, seven feed mills, two training
centers, and processing facilities for eel), vehicles and
construction equipment.
3.5     In addition, the project would include for both provinces vehicles
and equipment and local and overseas training and study tours.
C. Project Features in Jiangsu
Maricul=ur
3.6     Shrtm:  The proposed project would involve construction of about
3,960 ha of new ponds and improvement of about 4,300 ha of existing ponds
and would include water supply and drainage systems, power supplies,
access roads, farm buildings and offices. Criteria for site selection
were: 1) location within an existing sea dike (for flood protection), 2)
topography suitable for economical construction, 3) minimal requirements
for additional roads and power connections, 4) ability of the local
government to contribute to the proposed investment, and 5) willingness of
local farmers to participate in the project. Recent experience in the
province has shown that shrimp ponds with e water surface area of 2.4 to
2.7 ha, a water depth of about 2 m, and flushing rates to allow daily
replacement of about 10 percent of water volume are conditions for
efficient management and improved yields. Water temperature is also
critical as growth occurs only between 15 and 30 degrees C, and depth has
been recognized as a very important factor in stabilizing water
temperature. Ponds built to the above standards have realized higher
yields due to better water quality and an extended growing period in the
autumn without the growth cessation and mortality associated with ahigh
summer temperatures.  Existing ponds, typically about 1 m deep and up to
25 ha in *irea, would be improved by reducing the size, increasing the
depth and upgrading water supply facilities to facilitate better pond
management and control of water quality and temperature.



- 12 -
3.7    Ponds would be manually excavated, with earth placed around the
perimeter to form dikes. Dike sideslopes would be generally 2.5-3.0
horizontal to 1 vertical.  Freeboard of about 0.7 to 1.0 m above the
nominal full water level would be provided. Dike stability would be
enhanced in many designs by providing a ledge about 4 m wide on the inside
of the dike at a height of about 1 m above the floor of the pond. Surface
protection against water erosion is not generally necessary, but the
project would make provision for stone armour protection at problem areas.
3.8    For new sites, the project would include pumping stations, main
and branch canals providing direct supply to each pond, inlet and outlet
gates, and complementary drainage systems. For sites to be improved, it
would include additional pumping capacity, upgraded inlet and outlet gates
and culverts, and in some cases, new sea dike gates and sea canals.
Control gates in the sea dikes would adjust sea water inflow at high tide
and outflow at low tide. Since the slope of the shore is very flat, some
sites would require excavation of a sea canal to convey water across the
tidal flats toward the sea gates. In Nantong and Yancheng, sea water
would flow through the sea gates into a forebay and then be pumped into
canals for gravity distribution to ponds. The forebay would act as a
reservoir for water to be used during low tide hours and also permit a
degree of desilting. Commonly, the forebays must be dredged every few
years. In Lianyungang, water would be lifted into the project canals at
pumping stations situated in the sea dikes. Drainage to the sea at low
tide would be achieved by gravity flow. Drainage water would not be
allowed to mix with inflowing water. Some project sites would also
provide for freshwater from adjacent irrigation systems to adjust the
salinity of the pond water (salinity of about 20% is considered optimum)
or to insure continuity of supply on occasions when pumping is
interrupted.
3.9    About 280 km of electrical transmission lines and 63 substations
would be provided to connect with the rural electrificat'on system already
in place in the project areas. About 140 km of simple roads would be
constructed to connect the farms to existing county and provincial road
systems. These would generally be 1 - 2 km long and 4 m wide with a
gravel surface. About 53,000 sq m of dormitories, offices and workshops
would be constructed on the farms.
3.10    Five new feed mills, each with a capacity of 1,000-3,000 t/year,
would be established and seven existing mills would be renovated. The
feed mills would be equipped with separate units for grinding, mixing,
pelleting and crumbling, and the pellet mill would be installed with a
steam conditioner and a mixer for adding fat, oil or other binders to
produce a durable pellet. Adequate storage would be provided at each mill
for ingredients to be procured in the off-production season and for
stocking production early in the season to meet higher demands later. At
full development, the total feed requirement for about 8,260 ha of new and
rehabilitated ponds is estimated to be 67,000 t per season, based on a
shrimp yield of 1,950 kg/ha and a feed conversion factor of 4.15. Feed
requirements would be met by the new mills (12,000 t), mills to be
improved under the project (13,000 t) and existing mills in the project
area in satisfactory condition (20,000 t), with the remaining 22,000 t to
be made up by additional investment or to be eliminated by improvements in
the feed conversion factor. Because the shrimp growing season in



- 13 -
Jiangsu is from May through August, only 125 days would be needed for
shrimp feed production; the mills would produce animal or fish feed during
the rest of the year.
3.11    Feed formulation is a major constraint to increased shrimp
yields. The present practice is to feed pellets, produced by on-farm
mills from sun-dried trash fish, shrimp heads, oilseed cake and grain,
supplemented with loose raw or dried fish and molluscs. With the project,
the municipalities would contract with local research institutes to
provide feed formulations taking into account availability of local
materials and eonditions.
3.12    An additional constraint to efficient production of quality Shrimp
in China is inadequate refrigeration after harvesting. The harvested
product is transported, generally with insufficient or no ice, to cold
storage facilities for processing and a 6-14 hour freezing process. The
project would address this shortcoming by providing about 14 cold stores
with block ice plants at locations in the project area where existing
facilities are inadequate. Total capacity would be 5,300 t, ranging from
100 to 3000 t. Modern technology, including contact freezing, would be
introduced to raise product quality and energy efficiency.
3.13    The project would provide for construction and equipping of shrimp
culture training, research and extension centers at Lianyungang, Nantong
and Yancheng. The Lianyungang Center would expand existing facilities at
the Municipal Aquaculture Company's Da Ban Chao Aquaculture Farm;
construction under the project would include 2,600 sq m of buildings, a
hatchery and outdoor experimental ponds. In addition, office and
laboratory equipment would be provided. The Center will make use of
personnel of the Lianyungang Municipal Fishery Research Institute and the
Lianyungang Fishery School to conduct training, technical services and
research in shrimp culture. Special courses will be held for training the
technical staff of project shrimp farms. The Nantong Technical Extension
and Service Center would be established as an additional facility at the
existing Nantong Municipal Fishery Sciences and Technclogy Research
Institute to conduct training and research in laver, eel and shrimp
culture. In Yancheng, the project would provide for construction and
equipping of a municipal-level technical service center at the Xiangshui
County Development Company.
3.14    gkI:   The proposed project would take advantage of the local
supply of elvers (young eel)--Jiangsu has the largest elver supply in
China with annual catches of 10 t--and deep-well warm water sources to
develop 33 ha of open eel ponds and 87,000 sq m of enclosed ponds at 23
sites. About 10 ha of the open ponds would be based on using power plant
cooling water for heated water. Enclosed eel ponds would be used for
nurseries and overwintering in conjunction with open ponds used for
grow-out during warm weather. Enclosed ponds would be constructed as
clusters of reinforced concrete tanks which support superstructures
comprising a light metal framework covered by polyethylene film. Though
the main heat sources would be warm well water and solar energy,
supplementary coal-fired water heating systems would be installed. Since
continuous operation of water pumps and aerators is critically important
in intensive eel culture, standby generators would be provided. Regional
demand for eel feed is currently met by a combination of a small industry



- 14 -
in Shanghai and imports from Japan. The project would provide one 2000-t
capacity feed mill in Nantong. Technical service centers catering to
shrimp production would also be used for eel.
3.15    Laygr:  The proposed project would establish about 275 ha of laver
fields outside the sea dikes in Nantong where sea conditions and tidal
currents are favorable. The production cycle for laver includes seeding
on nets suspended in indoor nursery tanks and grow out on nets mounted
onto bamboo rafts (10-20/raft) anchored in shallow waters in the lower
part of the intertidal mudflat. The project would provide buildings and
tanks for the indoor nursery stage of growth, rafts, nets, poles and
pilings for outdoor growing racks, and automatic drying and packaging
equipment to produce a quality finished product.
Animal Husbandry
3.16    In Yancheng, the project would support the production of goats,
minks, rabbits, ducks and fish, mainly as sideline activities for
households already engaged in agriculture. These activities would utilize
underemployed family labor, crop residues, and naturally occurring
grasses. The project would provide initial breeding stock, on-farm
infrastructure, and veterinary facilities. In addition, it would provide
for construction and equipping of a Municipal Education Center in
Yancheng.
3.17    Goats: Goat production, using the local white breed derived from
the Guizhou white, would be based on availability of some 82,000 ha of
grassland with a wide range of coarse and fibrous plants better utilized
by goats than other ruminants. The project would provide improved
breeding stock (60,000 females and 1,500 males), laboratory and training
equipment and buildings for 35 Artificial Insemination (AI) stations to be
associated with the township livestock/veterinary stations (one for every
two participating townships). The typical Al station would have 80 sq m
of laboratories, 110 sq m of goat pens and 25 sq m of dormitories and
offices. In addition, the project would provide 214,000 sq m of on-farm
goat pens and minor equipment (walking tractors and straw shredding
machines) for each participating township. The goats, grown mainly for
skins, would also provide the fresh meat required by the mink and
accelerate soil rehabilitation of the natural grasslands which would in
future be converted to crop land.
3.18   Mlnk: The project would promote the expansion of mink production
as a sideline activity for farm households by providing improved breeding
stock and upgrading facilities at four existing breeding farms under the
Mink Development Corporation. Some 10,000 disease-free animals (domestic
and foreign) would be purchased for basic breeding stock. The centrally
located breeding farms would receive laboratory and veterinary equipment,
sheds, warehouses and dormitories, and cages. A mobile veterinary station
would be equipped to support high quality production by participating
households. Since all households would be located within a 10-20 km
radius, centralized facilities can readily provide feed, extension, and
veterinary services. The main rationale for including this component in
the project is the availability of suitable feed (trash fish, goat and
rabbit offal) and an existing industry of fairly high standard.



- 15 -
3.19    Rabbits:  Rabbit production has been included in the project
because it offers quick returns on investments, utilizes the abundant
grasses in the coastal region, and does not require specialized labor.
Two existing livestock farms would be modified to include provisions for
foundation breeding stock, minor grass land improvement, and additional
equipment. In addition, the project would provide on-farm works including
pens, hutches and upgrading of forage land. Some 52 townships, each with
about 160 households, would participate in the project. Each township
veterinary station would receive laboratory and veterinary equipment to
support household production facilities.
3.20    Ducks/Fish:  The duck/fish component would include establishment
of a hatchery to provide improved breeds of ducks, 267 ha of pond
construction or rehabilitation, and 20,000 sq m of pens. Ponds would be
0.6 ha and stocked for carp polyculture. The ducks (Cherry Hill breed)
would be grown for meat and down; their manure would fertilize the fish
ponds, reducing the requirements for supplemental fish feed. A Technical
Service Station would be constructed and provided with simple laboratory
equipment to provide extension services to the 400 households
participating in the project.
3.21    Agro-LDocessiLg:  The project would provide the following
processing facilities to meet the needs of the animal husbandry component:
coats ^   establishment of a slaughterhouse with an annual capacity of 1
million animals (located in Dafeng);
- expansion and improvement of an existing tannery, presently
producing pigskin leather, to produce 800,000 goat hides
annually (located in Dongtai);
Ducks -   establishment of a slaughter plant with annual capacity of 2
million birds and auxiliary facilities for production of 36 t/yr
high quality down (located in Sheyang);
-   improvement and expansion of a meat canning factory, including
a can making line, to increase production from 10,000 to 15,000
t canned duck meat (located in Yancheng);
- improvement and expansion of an existing down factory to produce
an additional 50,000 pieces of down garments (located in
Yancheng);
Rabbits-  expansion of a fur factory to increase production from 10,000 to
40,000 rabbit fur garments (located in Dafeng);
Other -   establishment (one) and expansion of an existing (one) feed mill
for producing 40,000 t of feed for various livestock (located
respectively in Sheyang and Xiangshui) and establishment of one
feed mill for producing mink feed (Dongtai).



^ 16 -
3.22    The project would support the expansion of several locally
well-proven fruit and nut crops around the Lianyungang area by financing
initial investments in planting material, fertilizer, labor and other
inputs. Both organic and chemical fertilizers would be used for crop
production. The project would provide for procurement of some 1,000 t of
chemical fertilizers required for crop production during the project
implementation period. An assurance was obtained at negotiations that
adequate quantities of chemical fertilizer nutrients would be procured and
made available to farmers and that an annual plan for such provision would
be prepared and submitted to the Bank group for review prior to November 1
of each year.
3.23    Hawthorn:  Considered a health food, hawthorn it a northern crop,
particularly tolerant of poor soils. The proposed project would be
located in a hilly area in western Ganyu county; it would include
substituting an improved variety (Big Golden Star) for old ones on 300 ha
of 4-5 year old plantations and selective replanting (filling in the gaps)
on 3,200 ha. Planting density would be about 750 trees/ha where varieties
are substituted and about 65 trees/ha in the replanted area. Altogether
some 30 village-owned plantations would be involved. The project would
provide fertilizer, labor and seedlings. In addition, township service
stations, which provide extension services and marketing information,
would be constructed and equipped for each of the nine participating
townships.
3.24    Gingkg:  The Gingko nut is a Chinese specialty, believed to have
nutritional and medicinal value. The proposed project would be located in
Pixian County in the northern tip of Jiangsu province. About 540 ha of
plantations would be established with short-stalk, low-crown seedlings at
a density of about 1,600 plants/ha. Grain, mainly barley, would be
intercropped on about 8,830 ha using more mature 3-m high seedlings at a
density of about 90 plants/ha. The project would provide chemical
fertilizer, labor, seedlings, and a l,000-t cold storage facility.
3.25    Chestnuts:  The project would establish about 1,300 ha of
chestnuts in western Donghai County. Planting density would be about
1,650 plants/ha; peanuts would be intercropped for the first four years.
At present, chestnut storage is carried out by burying in sand after the
late autumn harvest and reasonable quality can be maintained until about
January. With the l,000-t cold store to be provided under the project,
storage periods would be extended up to March or April. The project would
also provide chemical fertilizers, labor and seedlings.
3.26    Orchards:  A 2,000 ha fruit tree base, comprising 1,200 ha of
apples, 600 ha of peaches, and 200 ha of pears would be planted in Binhai
County. Fruit varieties have been selected on the basis of trials in an
existing 1,400 ha of orchards in the area, of which 700 ha are already in
production. About 60 participating villages would each develop 30-40 ha
orchards, contracting with specialized households for management of each
0.2-0.5 ha. The project would provide seedlings, labor, chemical
fertilizer, planting material and a fruit storage house.



- 17 -
3.27     Grateg:  About 540 ha of grapes would be established on eight
county-owned plantations in Donghai County. Planting material would be
obtained from the Botanical Research Institute of the Chinese Academy of
Sciences and the National Grape Research Institute in Shandong. The
project would include completion of minor irrigation works (a nearby
reservoir would be the water source) and provision of labor, seedlings,
fertilizers, and concrete posts and wires to support the vines.
3.28     Agro-Drocessing:  The project would also include construction of
the following processing facilities to meet the needs of the agriculture
component:
Grapes -   construction of a grape juice plant with a capacity of 3,200 t
per year (located in Donghai); and
Hawthorn - construction of a hawthorn processing plant with a capacity of
3,000 t of juice, 200 t jelly and 130 t pcwder.
Agriculture Technology Development
3.29     This component consists of eight subprojects selected by the
Jiangsu Technology Research and Development Institute and aimed at testing
innovative technology approaches in various fields of agricultural
production and processing. It would provide answers vital to
strengthening the linkages between research, development and
commercialization of these approaches not only in Jiangsu Province but
also of great importance to other areas in China. The subprojects are
described in Annex 2 and summarized below:
two shrimp feed mills based on new formulae, one involving
enzymatic digestion of fish and shrimp waste;
a mink feed mill using feed with a primarily vegetable protein
basis in addition to animal protein;
a rapeseed processing plant using newly patented Canadian
technology to detoxify oil and meal and render it useful for
human and animal consumption;
expansion of sesbania planting (a salt-tolerant soil improving
legume) in newly reclaimed tidal lands, not only for land
reclamation but primarily for production of glue from sesbania
seeds, and expansion of an existing gum powder plant;
planting of improved barley varieties suitable for malting and
constructing a malt plant;
production of improved asparagus varieties using modern
biotechnology methods and construction of a processing plant for
fresh (packaged), quick frozen and canned asparagus; and
production of serology test kits for fast and accurate
identification of animal and plant diseases, particularly
viruses.



- 18 -
Vehicles
3.30     The project would provide about 268 vehieles, ranging from 1.75-t
to 8-t capacity, to meet the annual transport volumes of aquatic,
livestock and agricultural production. Specialized vehicles, such as cold
storage trucks and heavy trucks, would be provided to cold stores, feed
mills, technical service centers and agroprocessing plants, and transport
vehicles would be made available to farms. Workboats and small tractors
would be provided to farmers.
Training and Technical Assistance
3.31     Training activities would focus on the mariculture component,
particularly shrimp production, by providing some 2,500 manmonths of local
training for farmer-producers and about 63 manmonths of overseas study
tours for project staff. The project includes about four manmonths of
technical assistance for the agriculture technology development component
and funds for purchase of patent rights. For agricultural and animal
husbandry components, local training for producers would be provided.
During negotiations, the details and schedule of the proposed training
program (Annex 5) were reviewed and an assurance was obtained that the
training component would be carried out in accordance with a schedule
acceptable to the Bank Group.
D. Project FeAtures in Zheiiang
Maricult=X
3.32     Shrimp:  The proposed project in Zhejiang would provide for
construction, completion or upgrading of sea dikes, gates and drainage
channels to enclose and drain 1,840 ha of tidal flats at five different
sites. Three sites--Dingshan, Shepan, and Wumen--are administered by the
Zhejiang Tidal Land Reclamation Corporation and are referred to
collectively as the Newly Enclosed Tidelands (NET); at these areas
construction of the reclamation dikes and gates is ongoing and the project
would provide for completion. The fourth site, Kaomen, located on Daishan
Island, is already fully enclosed, but some additional strengthening of
the dikes would be carried out under the project. The fifth site, Damutu,
would be the only site on which work has not yet begun; the proposed
project would cover Damutu Stage I or about half the area to be eventually
developed.
3.33     Generally, each site would require construction of a considerable
length of dike in shallow water and a short closure dike in an area where
water depths at high tide are up to 7.5 m. The closure dikes must
withstand the high tidal velocities of ebb and flow through a nearly
closed embankment or they may be located in deeper water in an exposed
situation where much more severe wave conditions must be withstood. The
maximum height of a closure dike would be about 12 m. Construction of
dikes on these very soft foundations is challenging; the soil has very low
bearing capacities and under loading exhib.ts very large consolidation.
At some locations, allowances of up to 3 m have been made for settlement
of the dike after construction. The design standard for the proposed



- 19 -
project (for a one in 10- or 20-year storm) is the same as used on
existing reclamation projects and is justified on the basis that even
though there has been damage to existing projects during typhoons, there
has been no breaching of the sea dikes and the damage is slow and
progressive and allows for ample warning. Also, no habitation or
important public services are permitted to be located within the area
protected by the outermost dikes.
3.34     Within the reclaimed areas, 1,382 ha would be developed for
shrimp ponds. Ponds would be supplied with seawater and drained by
separate canal systems. The sea gates for incoming water would be sited
away from harbors and other potential sources of pollution and at some
distance from the outflow gates. The ponds would be equipped for a
flushing rate of 30-50% of their volume per day; these high rates would be
required only on the hottest days and during growth periods. Tidal flows
would provide most of the energy necessary for flushing, but some pumping
would be required during neap tide periods (occurring at the first and
third quarters of the moon). The ponds at the highest elevations would
use pumps for less than 20 days per month, and those lower, even less.
Typically, about one-third of the pond area at a project site can be
flushed without any pumping.
3.35     A typical pond would have a water surface 100 m x 270 m (2.7
ha). It would be enclosed by a 2 m high embankment formed with steep side
slopes of 1.5-2 horizontal to 1 vertical. Water depth would vary from 1.5
to 2 m, except in a 10 m (width) x 1 m (depth) trench located about 10 m
from the dike. The internal geometry and water flushing rates are
different from the Jiangsu project. The greater water exchange capacity
follows from the fact that most of the water flow would be provided by
tidal action at no pumping cost. The higher rates of flushing provide a
means of temperature control making water depth less important and
favoring a simple form of construction which leaves the centers of the
ponds relatively shallow.
3.36     To meet feed requirements, feed mills would be provided at each
of four sites. Total capacity would be about 8,000 t--sufficient to meet
the requirements of the project area. Shrimp farmers in Zhejiang are
presently without adequate supplies of pelletized feed and about 80% of
shrimp feed is trash fish. Considerable amounts of feed are lost through
dissolution resulting in both low feed conversion rates and deterioration
of water quality. With properly formulated pelletized feed, conversion
efficiency would be increased, water pollution would be reduced, and unit
shrimp yield could be increased. Five cold stores, with capacities
ranging from 100 to 500 t, would be provided, one at each site.
3.37     uls:  The project would provide for establishment of 42 ha of
warm flowing-water ponds and 91 ha of cold still-water ponds for eel
cultivation. Warm water systems, using water from wells or industrial
cooling systems, would have flow rates to allow exchange of 100 percent or
more of tLe pond volume per day. Cold water systems, using unheated
surface water and operating seasonally from March to October, would have
water exchange rates of about 33 percent per day in the operating season.
In the cool season, the water depth would be increased and water exchange
minimized. Segregated water inflow and outflow channels would serve each
pond. Ponds would be 600 - 1200 sq m in area and about 0.9 m deep.



- 20 -
Support facilities would include two feed mills, with a total capacity of
3,000 t, and an export holding facility, in which to condition and package
eel for live shipment. In addition, the project would provide a roast eel
plant and a small plant to produce the specialized cartons to be used for
shipping eel overseas.
yehicleas and Eguigment
3.38     The project would provide, in addition to the usual vehicles for
production farm use, construction equipment to carry out nomplete
reclamation of the Damutu site. Requirements in Zhejiang call for about
141 vehicles, to be distributed between farms and support facilities such
as technical service centers, feed mills and cold stores. In addition,
workboats and small garden tractors would be provided to farmers.
Training and Technical Assistane
3.39     The project would provide training to upgrade the skills of local
development corporation and project office personnel end introduce them to
new technology in shrimp production, farm management and processing.  The
project includes 873 manmonths of medium- and long-term training (ranging
from five months to two years) at local colleges, 1,500 manmonths of
training for farmers, and 70 manmonths of overseas study tours and
training. It also includes funds for research contracts on feed
formulation, and production and processing technology (Annex 5). During
negotiations, the details and schedule of the proposed training program
were reviewed and an assurance was obtained that the training component
would be carried out in accordance with a schedule acceptable to the Bank
Group.
E. Status of Proiect Preparation
3.40     In Jiangsu, sites for the fisheries subprojects have been
approved by the provincial Bureau of Aquatic Products (BAP) on the basis
of surveys carried out by the township and county engineers; each county
(BAP or Bureau of Water Resourses) is preparing its final designs.   The
cost estimates are based on model designs for some sites and on prices
from current construction work in the local areas. In Zhejiang, planning
for the reclamation work is well advanced. The Bureau of Water Resources
engineers are experienced in the development of reclamation projects.
Site surveys and foundation investigations have been carried out at all
five sites, with laboratory tests of foundation soil samples included in
feasibility reports. Final design and construction drawings for the first
year's work in both project areas were undertaken between appraisal and
negotiations, and pond. excavation commenced in late 1987. The provincial
project offices have been set up and key staff have been appointed. The
training and technical assistance programs were agreed at negotiations.
F. Imnlementation Schedule
3.41     The Jiangsu component would be implemented over a period of four
years beginning in late 1987 with completion in late 1991. Mariculture,



- 21 -
animal husbandry components, fruit and nut plantation establishment, and
all processing facilities with the exception of the grape juice plant
would be completed in three years. In Zhejiang, the project would take
somewhat longer on account of the construction of sea dikes. Shrimp ponds
and supporting facilities would be carried out in two years following the
initial closure of the reclamation dikes at each site. Except for Damutu,
all subprojects would be completed by the end of 1990; Damutu would be
completed in 1992. A detailed implementation schedule is given in Fig. 1.
G. Cost Esti.tes
3.42     The total project cost in December 1987 prices is estimated at
US$217 million, with a foreign exchange component of US$102 million or 47%
of the total. .The total cost of the Jiangsu component is estimated to be
US$158.7 million, with a foreign exchange component of US$73.5 million
(46% of the total) and the Zhejiang component, US$58.3 million, with a
foreign exchange component of US$28.5 million (49% of the total). This
cost includes about US$500,000 in local taxes (at a rate of 10% on Jiangsu
agro-processing facility buildings); imported materials and equipment are
exempt from duties. Cost estimates are based on quantities derived from
the designs described in para. 3.41 and unit prices currently prevailing
in the project area. Prices for materials and equipment are based on
suppliers' quotations. Physical contingencies range from 5-15% of civil
works and equal 8% of base uosts. Price escalation for both foreign and
local costs when expressed in US dollars is based on annual international
price escalation rates for all goods and services of 1% in 1988-90 and
3.5% in 1991-93; and when expressed in yuan, is based on price escalation
rates of 6.5% in 1988-90 and 4.5% in 1991-92. Price contingencies would
amount to 2% of total costs expressed in US dollars. Estimated costs are
summarized in Table 3.2 and details are given in Annex 3.

I.  Prcuewmaent
3.44       Procurement arrangements are summarized in Table 3.3.  Works worth
about US$147.7 million would be required for the project. The Government
policy is to use labor-intensive methods wherever possible. This procedure is
particularly suitable for pond construction, plantation establishment and
on-farm works (US$108.0 million or 73% of total works). Townships would
directly carry out pond construction, contracting with local labor teams.
Townships and villages would contract with local farmers for plantation
establishment, ar4 farmers themselves would carry out the on-farm works under
animal husbandry, .ainly conutruction of animal pens.  Civil works for sea
dikes, cold stores, feed mills, technical service centers, and processing
plants, amounting to US$39.7 million (27%), would be procured through local
competitive bidding (L ') using procedures that have been reviewed and found
acceptable to the Bank    .ace these works are scattered geographically and
spread over time, they would not attract foreign attention.
3.45     Goods worth about US$67.9 million would be required for the project.
Whenever possible, machinery and equipment will be grouped into contracts
valued at US$200,000 or more and procured through ICB according to Bank Group
Guidelines. This will include the main agro-processing machinery (US$15.6
million), construction materials (US$9.9 million), vehicles (US$8.4 million),
feed and fertilizer (US$7.9 millio,.) worth a total of US$41.8 million (628 of
the total value of goods). Qualtfied domestic manufacturers would receive a
preference of 15% of c.i.f. bid price or applicable custom duties, whichever is
less, in bid evaluation. Contracts for goods valued at less than US$200,000
will be purchased through LCB using procedures that have been reviewed and
found acceptable to the Bank; this will include accessory equipment-for feed
mills, cold stores and processing plants, workboats, and small farm equipment
totalling US$12.6 million (19% of goods). Contracts for items of less than
$50,000 and other specified off-the-shelf items, subject to the Bank Group's
approval, would be procured through international and local shopping. This
would include breeding stock (US$2.8 million), fish meal (US$4.8 million),
individual pieces of construction equipment (US$1.0 million), and selected
equipment for the agricultural technology development component and small items
of laboratory and train3ng equipment (US$3.4 million), which would be procured
by directly soliciting bids of all known suppliers, both local and foreign.
However, the breeding stock, fish meal and a majority of the other items are
only available from foreign suppliers.
3.46     Training and technical assistance requiring foreign exchange
($800,000) would be financed by the Bank and subject to the Bank's prior
review. The remaining training requirements would be contracted for locally
and financed by the Goverment.
3.47     Preparation of bid documents would be carried out by the China
National Machinery Import and Export Corporation (CMIEC), an agency responsible
for ICB procurement in China and which has carried out this function for
previous Bank group projects. Bid invitation and evaluation and award
recommendations would be the responsibility of CMIEC in consultation with the
provincial authorities.
